\newcommand{\storybox}[3]{% #1=x, #2=y, #3=text
  \begin{textblock}{3}(#1,#2)
    \noindent%
    \begin{tikzpicture}
      \node[rectangle, rounded corners=3pt, fill=white, inner sep=0.1in, text width=2.55in, align=left] {%
        \small\sffamily #3%
      };
    \end{tikzpicture}%
  \end{textblock}%
}

{\Huge\sffamily\bfseries No Time to Discourse}

\vspace{0.5in}

{\Large\sffamily A Speculative Atlas of Climate Disaster}

\vspace{0.5in}

{\large\sffamily A Procedurally Generated Novel}

\vspace{1in}

{\large\sffamily by Mark Sample}

\vfill

{\normalsize\sffamily Generated November 24, 2025}

\end{titlepage}

% About page
\newpage
\section*{About This Novel}

\noindent\textit{No Time to Discourse} is a speculative atlas that explores climate disaster across North America through interactive mapping and generative flash fiction.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent This novel was generated for NaNoGenMo (National Novel Generation Month), transforming the web-based interactive experience of https://notime.now/ into a print format. Each page combines watercolor maps from Stamen Design with works of flash fiction, which are procedurally-generated through bespoke RiTa.js grammars developed by Mark Sample.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent Each of the stories in this novel is a work of fiction, yet each also attempts to capture at a human level the realities of climate disaster.

\vspace{0.3in}

\noindent\textbf{Original Web Project:} \url{https://notime.now/}

\noindent\textbf{Code Repository:} \url{https://github.com/samplereality/no-time-to-discourse-novel}

\clearpage

% Henry V quote on its own page
\vspace*{\fill}
\begin{center}
  {\Large\textit{"The day is hot, and the weather, and the wars, and the King,\\
  and the Dukes; it is no time to discourse."}}

  \vspace{0.3in}

  --- Henry V
\end{center}
\vspace*{\fill}

\storybox{3.88}{1.59}{\textbf{Richmond, Indiana}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Wednesday, March 4, 2026}\\
 The storm came on fast. The sky over Richmond turned black. Eva had a fleeting thought, that she had left her soccer ball outside. We had no gas, no heat, no lights. They trucked in bottled water, since nothing was safe to drink.}

\storybox{0.53}{1.16}{\textbf{Muncie, Indiana}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Friday, January 14, 2028}\\
 The storm isn't even over before the stream bursts its banks, the water rising 49 feet and swamping parts of Muncie. It's bad enough when Saoirse sees Delaware Country Club wash away, but then she hears  about the playground. Twenty missing.}

\storybox{5.06}{4.90}{\textbf{Marion, Indiana}\\[0.1in]
\textit{Tuesday, November 24, 2026}\\
 Rank dark water swamps Jocelyn's basement. A frozen ravioli bobs in the dark water. Tripp boils his water before cooking. The storm didn't even have a name, he thinks. Rescue teams are tired, so tired. }

 Tuktoyaktuk is flooded with refugees. They trudge in pulling wagons full of useless thingscedar chests, chairs, hearing aids. They come from the cities, the towns. Seattle. Philadelphia. Places too broken to fix.}

 The storm came on fast, like a bolt of lightning. The sky over Grand Rapids darkened. Serenity had a fleeting thought, that she had left her street light outside. The clocks stopped at 10:28 AM. They trucked in bottled water, since nothing was safe to drink.}

Cedric watched as the storm lashed against his windows. Meanwhile Mustafa spins up his TikTok channel, ranting about solar radiation management. A thousand views and counting.}

It's been eleven months since rain. The towns are dying. Tech executives tweet about water conservation from their rooftop infinity pools.}
